**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is May, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

Brief explanation of borderline decisions and adjustments:
1. For articles about same‐sex marriage (ID 1) and trans policy (IDs 16, 25, 75), I used Topic 5.1 under Civil Rights since the focus is on LGBTQ+ rights.
2. Articles dealing with government funding cuts (IDs 3, 4, 9, 15, 19, 20, 29, 81, 83, 88) were sorted into Federal Budget and Program Cuts with the subtopics chosen to best reflect whether the focus was on science/research, environmental/public lands, or social programs.
3. Trade, tariffs, taxes, and monetary matters (IDs 26, 28, 30, 31, 32, 33, 34, 35, 37, 55, 56, 57, 58, 59, 68, 94, 95, 96) were placed under Economic and Trade Policy with selection among tariff agreements, tax policy, financial markets, or cryptocurrency as appropriate.
4. Immigration news (IDs 10, 42, 48, 63, 78, 82, 89, 90, 93) were assigned mostly to Immigration and Border Policy; for cases such as legal immigrants (ID 78), I used Visa/Legal Immigration while deportations went under Enforcement.
5. Coverage of congressional battles, hearings, confirmations, and political maneuvers (IDs 11, 12, 13, 27, 43, 47, 49, 51, 54, 60, 62, 65, 71, 73, 85, 92, 97) were all placed in Legislative Affairs and Political Dynamics with selection among internal dynamics, legislative negotiations, or political strategy.
6. Judicial topics, including Supreme Court decisions and legal challenges (IDs 10, 14, 18, 22, 41, 61, 64, 70, 87) appear under Judiciary and International Relations.
7. Finally, items focused on presidential nominations or his rhetoric (IDs 44, 50, 52, 66, 67, 69, 84, 86) were placed under Executive Branch Actions with the appropriate subtopic.

This completes Step 2.

# DAILY BRIEFING: MAY 2025

## 1. FEDERAL BUDGET AND PROGRAM CUTS

### 1.1 Research and Science Funding
The Trump administration continues implementing substantial cuts to research institutions despite legal challenges. NIH research grants are being axed even after a judge blocked such cuts [1], while economists warn these reductions could have "dire consequences for GDP" [2]. NASA faces significant budget reductions with implications for the space agency's operations [3]. 

The impact on the scientific community is immediate and severe—University of Washington scientists are cutting lab staff, and postdoctoral researchers are leaving the country as research funding diminishes [4]. These cuts represent a fundamental shift in federal priorities toward scientific research and development, with potential long-term implications for America's competitive position in global innovation.

### 1.2 Environmental and Public Lands
Federal environmental programs and public lands face reductions and potential privatization. House Republicans have approved an amendment authorizing the sale of public lands in Utah and Nevada [5], while the administration reportedly plans $26 million in cuts to national parks [6]. These actions signal significant changes in federal land management policy.

Beyond funding cuts, concerns about data preservation have emerged. Web archivists are racing to save U.S. public data amid fears of potential deletion of government information [7], highlighting worries about long-term access to environmental and scientific records.

### 1.3 Agency Restructuring and Social Services
The administration is eliminating or significantly restructuring multiple federal agencies and programs. Coal miners in West Virginia have lost access to black lung screenings following cuts to the worker safety agency NIOSH [8]. After three decades of operation, the Energy Star program faces elimination [9], potentially impacting energy efficiency standards nationwide.

International aid cuts have drawn high-profile criticism. Bill Gates has publicly accused Elon Musk of "killing" children through USAID cuts [10] and announced plans to donate $200 billion over 20 years while expressing horror at U.S. foreign aid reductions [11]. Domestically, a bipartisan group of state lawmakers is calling on Congress to preserve the Head Start program [12], indicating that concerns about social service reductions cross party lines.

## 2. ECONOMIC AND TRADE POLICY

### 2.1 Tariffs and Trade Agreements
The Trump administration is reshaping U.S. trade relations through bilateral agreements and aggressive tariff policies. Multiple sources confirm an imminent trade deal with Britain [13][14], demonstrating the administration's preference for bilateral rather than multilateral agreements. Simultaneously, the U.S. is leveraging tariff threats in negotiations, pushing nations facing potential tariffs to approve Musk's Starlink services [15]. China has reportedly initiated planned trade meetings with Washington, while the administration considers exemptions for certain products like strollers [16].

Economic impacts of the tariff policy are becoming increasingly apparent across multiple sectors. Manufacturing supply chains face significant disruption, with semiconductor equipment makers warning of serious consequences for technology production [17]. Consumer prices are already rising, with Ford hiking prices on three vehicle models citing direct tariff impacts [18]. The agricultural sector also faces challenges, with analysis predicting small farms in MAGA heartlands will be hit hardest by tariff policies [19]. Internal tensions have emerged among labor leaders, with UAW officials in Michigan breaking with their national president on tariffs against Canada [20], highlighting regional differences in policy impact.

### 2.2 Financial Markets and Monetary Policy
The Federal Reserve is maintaining its independence despite executive branch pressure. The Fed has held interest rates steady, defying pressure from President Trump [21], who subsequently called Fed Chair Jerome Powell a "fool" for this decision [22]. Market responses have been volatile, with gold dropping over 1% following Powell's cautious statements [23].

In corporate developments, Tesla faces challenges in key European markets, with sales in Germany and the U.K. falling to their lowest point in two years [24]. Meanwhile, questions are emerging about the fiscal soundness of the administration's tax proposals, with the Washington Post reporting that the calculations "don't add up" [25].

### 2.3 Cryptocurrency Developments
Cryptocurrency initiatives are generating ethical concerns. A Trump-hosted cryptocurrency fundraising dinner, where plates reportedly cost $1.5 million, has drawn ethics scrutiny as the president could potentially profit from a related meme coin [26]. At the state level, Arizona Governor Katie Hobbs has signed legislation creating a Bitcoin reserve, just days after vetoing other cryptocurrency legislation [27], demonstrating varied approaches to digital currency regulation.

## 3. HEALTHCARE AND SOCIAL WELFARE

### 3.1 Medicaid and Health Insurance Programs
Congressional Republican leadership is navigating internal divisions over proposed Medicaid reductions. House Speaker Mike Johnson has ruled out aggressive cuts to Medicaid as moderate Republicans express reservations about such measures [28]. The Congressional Budget Office analysis has intensified these concerns, finding that millions of Americans could lose insurance under GOP Medicaid options being considered [29]. 

This has sparked significant resistance within the party, with centrist Republicans revolting against steep cuts to Medicaid and other programs included in legislation focused on tax breaks [30]. The healthcare debate represents one of the most visible areas of Republican internal disagreement in Congress, with potential implications for the broader legislative agenda.

## 4. EXECUTIVE BRANCH ACTIONS

### 4.1 Presidential Appointments and Personnel
President Trump is making notable appointments that signal administration priorities. Trump has nominated Dr. Casey Means, described as a doctor and influencer with close ties to RFK Jr., for the position of U.S. Surgeon General [31]. In the sports realm, former Alabama football coach Nick Saban is expected to join a presidential commission on college athletics [32], bringing his experience in collegiate sports to administration policy discussions.

### 4.2 Presidential Communications and Policy Directives
The president's public communications reveal evolving positions on key issues. Trump has changed his messaging on the economy [33], while directly criticizing former Transportation Secretary Pete Buttigieg for air traffic control problems [34]. The administration is also implementing significant changes to U.S. government media operations, planning to feed Voice of America with content from One America News (OAN) [35], representing a substantial shift in the editorial direction of this established government broadcaster.

## 5. IMMIGRATION AND BORDER POLICY

### 5.1 Enforcement Actions and Policy Shifts
Immigration enforcement actions have generated controversy regarding their targets and methods. Reports indicate that Trump's Border Czar secretly deported two U.S. citizen children [36], raising serious legal questions. Immigration enforcement has expanded to include educators, with Senator Schatz condemning an ICE raid on Filipino teachers in Maui as a "shameful abuse of power" [37]. Federal officials are reviewing the visa status of 80 individuals detained after participating in protests at Columbia University [38].

Economic analyses are highlighting potential consequences of restricting legal immigration. Bloomberg reports the U.S. economy would face significant losses if the administration proceeds with policies pushing out legal immigrants [39]. The administration's refugee resettlement priorities are undergoing changes, with an NPR report revealing plans specifically focused on resettling white South Africans [40]. Presidential rhetoric on border security has expanded beyond the southern border, with Trump developing a fixation on the U.S.-Canada border [41].

## 6. LEGISLATIVE AFFAIRS AND POLITICAL DYNAMICS

### 6.1 Congressional Challenges and Party Divisions
Senate Republicans face procedural and political challenges in advancing the administration's legislative agenda. The party is confronting budget reconciliation obstacles that could impact their ability to pass key legislation with a simple majority [42]. Senate Republicans confirmed Frank Bisignano to lead Social Security in a party-line vote, despite a whistleblower's allegation that he had improper contact with the agency to facilitate the onboarding of Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE) personnel [43].

House Republicans are experiencing significant infighting over what Trump has called his "big beautiful bill" [44], with GOP Representative Chip Roy demanding leadership "show us the math" regarding tax cuts and Medicaid proposals [45]. On the Democratic side, Senator John Fetterman is facing scrutiny following reports of an outburst at a meeting with union officials [46] that allegedly left staff crying. Reports indicate that Trump is elevating Senator Marco Rubio as both a potential successor and a 2028 rival to Vice President J.D. Vance [47], suggesting early positioning for the next presidential election cycle.

## 7. JUDICIARY AND INTERNATIONAL RELATIONS

### 7.1 Supreme Court Actions and Judicial Independence
The Supreme Court has allowed the Trump administration to enforce its ban on transgender troops in the military while cases proceed through the courts. Lower courts had previously blocked the policy, ruling it lacked supporting evidence and violated equal protection principles [48]. This decision comes amid tension between the judiciary and executive branch, with Chief Justice John Roberts making public statements defending judicial independence as essential for properly checking both Congress and the president [49].

### 7.2 Foreign Policy Challenges
The administration's approach to international crises is drawing scrutiny. CNN questions why President Trump is not leading emergency efforts to ease tensions in the escalating India-Pakistan crisis [50]. On Ukraine policy, Vice President Vance has stated that Russia is not being realistic regarding Ukraine, with Trump reportedly indicating he may agree with Vance's position [51]. According to an economist cited by the Kyiv Independent, "Ukraine is holding cards" that strengthen its position against U.S. pressure to make concessions [52].

## 8. CIVIL RIGHTS AND STATE POLICIES

### 8.1 LGBTQ+ Rights and Religious Freedom
LGBTQ+ rights face legislative challenges at multiple governmental levels. Oklahoma GOP legislators are asking the Supreme Court to overturn same-sex marriage, with Republicans in at least five other states introducing similar resolutions [53]. The White House's plan for transgender youth has drawn criticism from some advocates who question whether it amounts to "conversion therapy lite" [54]. Simultaneously, the administration is implementing policies regarding religious expression, with Axios reporting that Trump's push against "anti-Christian bias" is affecting federal workers [55].

### 8.2 State Policy Initiatives
States continue to advance significant policy changes independent of federal actions. Pennsylvania's House of Representatives has approved legislation to legalize adult-use cannabis [56], while Washington has become the third state to enact a rent cap law [57]. Universities remain sites of political conflict, with dozens of pro-Palestinian protesters arrested after Columbia University called in police to address campus demonstrations [58].
